  <span id="freeText17923651037440230824" style="display:none"><b>4 What-the-BLOODY-Hell Stars<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/639787.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>"It’s our actions that define us. What we choose. What we resist. What we’re willing to die for.[...]There are only shades of gray. Black and white are nothing more than lofty ideals in our minds, the standards by which we try to judge things, and map out our place in the world in relevance to them."</i></b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385407316ra/7143292.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>An obsessed man(?) with dangerous secrets.<br>A seductive prince with his own agenda.<br>A ruthless Grand Mistress.</i><br>And in the middle of this deadly game of chess where the lives of the pawns are insignificant, a no-longer innocent girl who was forced to be a woman that survives but she no longer recognizes.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385713727i/7208922.jpg" width="400" height="180" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When Mac traveled to Ireland to solve the mystery of her sister's brutal murder, she wasn't expecting a book to be responsible of the end of the world.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382641196ra/6086976.gif" width="400" height="267" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Sinsar Dubh</i> the long lost Fae book, written by the Unseelie King himself. A book wated by many and fatal as it is mysterious.<br><br>Thrust in a world of growing darkness and shadows, Mac is forced to build uneasy alliances and trust 2 men that they may be using her for their own purposes but somehow they keep saving her life.<br><br><b>
  <i>“If you think to stand between V’lane and me, and play both ends against the middle, you’ll get ripped to pieces. If I were you, Ms. Lane, I’d choose a side, and fast.”</i>
</b><br><br><b>V'lane</b> is the Fae, but <b>Jericho Barrons</b> holds all the secrets and is more dangerous to the the senses of the woman inside of the two.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385713727i/7208923._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="280" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>With no idea of the grand scheme of things, forced to see the events unfolding while Mac is narrating her story by memories tainted of blood and pain, this book held me transfixed. Dark, emotional and passionate, I couldn't put it down until the nail-biting end end even then I immediately started the next...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380432903ra/870782.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>WHY on earth haven't I started this series sooner???<br>I claim sheer stupidity.... Don't make the same mistake!!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17923651037440230824" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

That's just weird! Everyone knows that when you are kids, you pretend the floor is covered in HOT LAVA, and that is why you jump from beds to dressers to couches to tables, etc... There was even an epic episode of Community where Abed and Troy start a giant hot lava game at the school for Troy's last day. It was dean-tastic!<br><br>But, it figures that Mac would have a stupid name for the game. She can't even swear like a normal person. Idiot!<br><br>The action in this book does get better than the last and the dark characters are really interesting. I like the complexity of the story, and how it keeps growing as time goes on. Nothing ends too quickly or neatly, which is nice. And, Mac has gotten a tiny bit smarter, more so in the beginning of the book, but she has a long way to go to get to your average person's start point.<br><br>It seems pretty obvious, though, that Mac is still making way too many stupid assumptions. And, her stubbornness combined with her stupidly false bravado is going to keep getting her almost killed and waiting for Jericho to save her every book.</span>

But while the world is turning more evil, she is gaining more knowledge and strength and one thing she makes sure to never lose is: hope.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Hope is a critical thing. Without it, we are nothing. Hope shapes the will. The will shapes the world. I might have been suffering a dearth o</i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText556569614640554936" style="display:none"><br><b>4.5 *I LOVE THIS SERIES, AND BARRONS, AND MAYBE V'LANE A LITTLE TOO* STARS.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385847995i/7241542._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>More action, more suspense, more fear, more doubt, more evil, more darkness; all of these elements sure don't make Mac's life any easier. But while the world is turning more evil, she is gaining more knowledge and strength and one thing she makes sure to never lose is: hope.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Hope is a critical thing. Without it, we are nothing. Hope shapes the will. The will shapes the world. I might have been suffering a dearth of hope but I had a few things left: will, desperation in spades, and a chance."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385847995i/7241543._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Being touched by Jericho Barrons with kindness makes you feel like you must be the most special person in the world. It's like walking up to the biggest, most savage lion in the jungle, lying down, placing your head in its mouth and, rather than taking your life, it licks you and purrs."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385847995i/7241544.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Question: When you're one of the few people who can do something to fix a problem, just how responsible does that make you for it?<br>Answer: It's how you choose to answer that question that defines you."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>This second part of the series managed to captivate me once again from beginning to end, and it made me an even bigger fan of KMM and the brilliantly created world and characters in this series. It also left me with even MORE questions that I need answers to, so I'm moving on to the next part, <b>Faefever</b>, ASAP!!<br><br><b>~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*</b><br><br></span>

Something else entirely?), <br/>-what role does he play in the game (Is he bad?, Is he the enemy?, Will he help?) and<br/>-what he wants from Mac (To use her? To help her? To play with her before he eats her?)<br/><br/>So, what we learned about Barrons in this book :<br/><br/>HE IS EXTREMELY VOLATILE:<br/>“And yes, I trashed the bookstore when I couldn't find you. You'll have to choose a new bedroo</span>
  <span id="freeText12913887091981654363" style="display:none">The most interesting character of the series is definitely Jericho Barrons. There is this mystery of <br />-what is he exactly (Fae? Human? Something else entirely?), <br />-what role does he play in the game (Is he bad?, Is he the enemy?, Will he help?) and<br />-what he wants from Mac (To use her? To help her? To play with her before he eats her?)<br /><br />So, what we learned about Barrons in this book :<br /><br />HE IS EXTREMELY VOLATILE:<br />“And yes, I trashed the bookstore when I couldn't find you. You'll have to choose a new bedroom, too.”<br /><br />HE IS CRUDE WITH HIS EXPLANATIONS<br />“I'm sorry your pretty little world got all screwed up, but everybody's does, and you go on. It's how you go on that defines you.” <br />“I doubt he'll be a prince, Ms. Lane. Men rarely are.”<br /><br />HE IS EXCEPTIONALLY POSSESSIVE AND PROTECTIVE:<br />"And I am going to tattoo you, Ms. Lane, however and wherever I please.”<br />“If I have to chain you to a fucking wall to protect you from your own stupidity, I will!"<br /><br />HE REALLY DESIRES MAC:<br />“I know you're the one with boobs! They're in my fucking face every fucking time I turn around!”<br /><br />HE IS JEALOUS:<br />"Nice tan, Ms. Lane. So, where the fuck have you been for the past month?”<br /><br />HE ANTAGONIZES V'LANE:<br />“I am not like any other player in this game and I will never be like V'lane.”<br /><br />HE TRIES TO TEACH, WHEN MAC LETS HIM:<br />“I told you, Ms. Lane, never believe anything is dead-"<br />“One day you may kiss a man you can't breathe without, and find breath is of little consequence.”<br /><br />HIS SPECIES IS UNKNOWN:<br />“What are you Barrons?”<br />“The one who will never let you die, and that's more, Ms Lane, than anyone in your life has been able to say to you. More than anyone else can do.” <br /><br />The above characteristics will be noticed in the following books, too –TO THE EXTREME!</span>

<div id="review_2213663178" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2213663178" />
    <a title="K. Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17568354-k-elizabeth"><img alt="K. Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606078931p2/17568354.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2213663178?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K. Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K. Elizabeth" href="/user/show/17568354-k-elizabeth">K. Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/2705590-bloodfever">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=very-good-but-not-phenomenal">very-good-but-not-phenomenal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2213663178" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer386586585969441749"><b>3.5/5</b><br/><br/><i>Whoa,</i> that was quite a ride.<br/><br/><i>Bloodfever</i> was without a doubt better than <i>Darkfever</i> - but only by a half-star. Regardless, it wasn't an "average" read like its predecessor. Therefore, Karen Marie Morning is doing something right & I can't wait to see if book three will get better!<br/><br/>When I think of this series, what immediately comes to mind are the words: Guilty pleasure. Because that's what it is, to me. I can't pinpoint one "phenomenal" aspect within these first two books, however, I <i>can</i> tell </span>
  <span id="freeText386586585969441749" style="display:none"><b>3.5/5</b><br /><br /><i>Whoa,</i> that was quite a ride.<br /><br /><i>Bloodfever</i> was without a doubt better than <i>Darkfever</i> - but only by a half-star. Regardless, it wasn't an "average" read like its predecessor. Therefore, Karen Marie Morning is doing something right &amp; I can't wait to see if book three will get better!<br /><br />When I think of this series, what immediately comes to mind are the words: Guilty pleasure. Because that's what it is, to me. I can't pinpoint one "phenomenal" aspect within these first two books, however, I <i>can</i> tell you that I keep coming back for more. It's pretty addictive.<br /><br />Thankfully, Mac wasn't as annoying in this novel. I mean, she still was (it wouldn't be Mac if she didn't somehow bring up her outfit in the middle of battle), but she was <i>much</i> better. She even matured and acted more responsible. Go figure.<br /><br />Ah, of course I need to bring up Barrons. In book one, I didn't care whether or not he ended up with Mac, but in this book, I kept wondering <i>why</i> they weren't together yet. So obviously my subconscious wanted them together, but <i>I</i> was in denial or unaware of that. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Regardless, when they kissed (and more) in the cell after he came to rescue her, I was really exited and shocked at everything that had happened before the kiss, too. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Overall,</b> this series is still quite confusing. Seriously, each book only adds <i>more</i> questions than answers. However, that adds intrigue. So, yeah, smart thinking, Moning.</span>
  <a data-text-id="386586585969441749" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1814182370" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1814182370" />
    <a title="Fareya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22583912-fareya"><img alt="Fareya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485406498p2/22583912.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1814182370?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fareya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fareya" href="/user/show/22583912-fareya">Fareya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1814182370" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4016895546246904039">"<i>Question: When you're one of the few people who can do something to fix a problem, just how responsible does that make you for it?<br/>Answer: It's how you choose to answer that question that defines you.</i>"<br/><br/>This sure is one crazy, kickass series. The second installment, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/344262.Bloodfever' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bloodfever</a> flawlessly retains the addictive nature of the story. The plot is getting edgier, more dramatic and intense. With every page we get immersed deeper into the powerful and deadly world of Fae. <br/><br/>I used to think <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/112750.Darkfever' rel='nofollow noopener'>Darkfever</a> was fas</span>
  <span id="freeText4016895546246904039" style="display:none">"<i>Question: When you're one of the few people who can do something to fix a problem, just how responsible does that make you for it?<br />Answer: It's how you choose to answer that question that defines you.</i>"<br /><br />This sure is one crazy, kickass series. The second installment, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/344262.Bloodfever" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloodfever</a> flawlessly retains the addictive nature of the story. The plot is getting edgier, more dramatic and intense. With every page we get immersed deeper into the powerful and deadly world of Fae. <br /><br />I used to think <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/112750.Darkfever" rel="nofollow noopener">Darkfever</a> was fast paced, but in comparison, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/344262.Bloodfever" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloodfever</a> is a total rush. Oh, don't get me wrong, in no way is this hurried, but the sheer number of events that take place in such a narrow timeframe is absolutely appalling. Even though we are supplied with plenty of new information, much is left unanswered leaving the reader delirious with anticipation. Action-packed and jammed with suspense, this second book in the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/41192-fever" rel="nofollow noopener">Fever</a> series is an insane, wild ride that filled me with doubts and left me craving for more.<br /><br /><i>“It's a strange new world out there and the rules have changed: It's every princess for herself.”</i> <br /><br />Alongside the plot, the character development is progressing just right. Mac has come a long way in a short time. Accepting her gift as a sidhe-seer, she has grown into a stronger, more mature and determined young woman who can stand her ground. She is learning the ways of this world, getting smarter and coming out of her pink and pastel cocoon. Barrons, on the other hand remains an enigma. Dark and secretive, he still manages to be exasperatingly irresistible. Won't we all love to get more insight on this brooding, dangerous, antagonizing character of all times. Here's hoping in the next book maybe. At least we had a few intense, emotional scenes with Barrons and Mac. Talk about slow burn romance! <br /><br /><i>"One day you will kiss a man you can’t breathe without, and find breath is of little consequence."</i><br /><br />The Fae Prince, V'lane and his intentions are still a complete mystery to me. Manipulation is in his nature, he does not play fair and is extremely sly. I didn't like him anymore than I did in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/112750.Darkfever" rel="nofollow noopener">Darkfever</a>. Let's see what the future holds for him. As for secondary characters, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/344262.Bloodfever" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloodfever</a> has a fair share of some great ones. I particularly liked Dani. She has sass and exactly the right attitude towards life. I'd like to get to know her better. Same with Ryodan. Rowena, on the other hand seems like a ruthless and cunning person with her own agenda. I wonder what that is! Questions, questions!! And as if we didn't have enough questions, the ending too is a cliffhanger!<br /><br />Karen Marie Moning has done a brilliant job of weaving an intricate, enticing story that is getting better and more convoluted with every installment. On to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2702704-faefever" rel="nofollow noopener">Faefever</a> now, in hopes of getting some of those answers and uncovering a few mysteries. <br /><br /><i>"Hope is a critical thing. Without it, we are nothing. Hope shapes the will. The will shapes the world"</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4016895546246904039" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer190417453" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14503724292645454373">This review can also be found at <a href='http://carolesrandomlife.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Carole's Random Life</a>.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418086491i/12665553._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>5 Stars!<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Question: When you're one of the few people who can do something to fix a problem, just how responsible does that make you for it?<br/>Answer: It's how you choose to answer that question that defines you.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I really can't understand why I only gave this book 4 stars the last time that I read it. Basically, I think that any book that I feel compelled to read not once, not twice but 3 times (so far) has to deserve 5 stars...it just </span>
  <span id="freeText14503724292645454373" style="display:none">This review can also be found at <a href="http://carolesrandomlife.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Carole's Random Life</a>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418086491i/12665553._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>5 Stars!<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Question: When you're one of the few people who can do something to fix a problem, just how responsible does that make you for it?<br>Answer: It's how you choose to answer that question that defines you.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>I really can't understand why I only gave this book 4 stars the last time that I read it. Basically, I think that any book that I feel compelled to read not once, not twice but 3 times (so far) has to deserve 5 stars...it just has to be that way. I first came across this book at a yard sale along with two other books in the series. I paid 25¢ for it and still feel so lucky that I literally stumbled upon them. This series is an excellent example of why I am a reader. This world is real to be. I daydream about Barrons. When I hear songs mentioned in these books, I think about what was happening in the plot at the time. It really does not get much better than this.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I'd like to tell you that the monster under the bed is rarely as bad as you fear of it, but in my experience it's almost always worse.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418086491i/12665554._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Things get even a bit crazier in this book. Mac has had a lot to deal with in such a very short time. She is dealing better with everything she has found out about who and what she is in this installment in the series. She is smart and takes advice when she believes it will help her and really wants to learn. The monsters in this book get scarier and by the end of this book, she encounters some things that are completely frightening but she never gives up.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"What are you, Barrons?" "The one who will never let you die, and that's more, Ms. Lane, than anyone in your life has ever been able to say to you. More than anyone else can do."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>I cannot think of a character in a book that I like more than Barrons. He can be an ass and we really don't know that much about who or what he really is but he is the most appealing man that I have ever encountered on the page of a book. When things need to be done, Barrons is there to do them and he always seems to be in control. He is able to save the day even when things look hopeless. He says things that make me laugh, make me think, and sometimes make me want to think mushy thoughts. Barrons is reason enough to read this series.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"One day you may kiss a man you can't breathe without, and find breath is of little consequence."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>This book has some of the best lines. If you took some of these lines and shared them with others, they would never believe that it comes from a story like this. It's a different kind of book and makes you think at times. I think everyone should read this series. It is really that good. If you haven't read it yet, I urge you to pick up the first book in the series and get started right away. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418086491i/12665555._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="14503724292645454373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_416913690" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/416913690" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/416913690?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781423341949" href="/book/show/6695174-bloodfever">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer416913690" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2014586936883422142"><br/>It’s a little hard for me to write a review for Bloodfever, because I finished it and immediately started the audio of Faefever. I think I might confuse some of both books together if I try to summarize it for anyone. Suffice it to say that I’m hooked! <br/><br/>In Darkfever, Mac was a spoiled, naïve, and innocent young woman out to find her sister, Alina’s murderer. In Bloodfever, Mac has grown up a bit, whether she wanted to or not. She’s still the old-fashioned southern, pink, and sparkle clad woman wh</span>
  <span id="freeText2014586936883422142" style="display:none"><br />It’s a little hard for me to write a review for Bloodfever, because I finished it and immediately started the audio of Faefever. I think I might confuse some of both books together if I try to summarize it for anyone. Suffice it to say that I’m hooked! <br /><br />In Darkfever, Mac was a spoiled, naïve, and innocent young woman out to find her sister, Alina’s murderer. In Bloodfever, Mac has grown up a bit, whether she wanted to or not. She’s still the old-fashioned southern, pink, and sparkle clad woman when she can be, but she’s no longer as innocent as she was. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>Mac: “I would wear pink because I knew my future was anything but rosy. I would accessorize myself to the hilt, and I would wear flirty shoes because my world needed more beauty to counter all the ugliness in it. I would wear pink because I hated gray, I didn’t deserve white, and I was sick of black.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Bloodfever follows Mac in her quest to find the Unseelie book, the Sinsar Dubh, her dying sister’s last wish, with Barrons. She still has no idea what Barrons motives are in finding the ancient and powerful book, but at the moment he’s been the most helpful of all the big players, saving her life a couple of times. She still keeps V’lane in her back pocket, but at arms length because he’s a death-by-sex Fae prince (not a horrible way to go, IMO, but still), and she’s not about to trust him fully. I, like Mac wouldn’t trust Rowena any farther than I could throw that old witch! She’s left her high and dry too many times for my liking! <br /><br />I like the direction Mac and Barron’s relationship is taking, and whether they admit it to each other or themselves, you can tell they’re beginning to matter to one another. Love this quote because it’s so no-nonsense and oh-so-Barrons:<br /><br /><b>
  <i> “What are you Barrons?”<br />“The one who will never let you die, and that’s more, Ms. Lane, than anyone in your life has been able to say to you. More than anyone else can do.” </i>
</b><br /><br />This is like a love letter from Barrons. He may not utter words of endearment to Mac, but you can tell she’s burrowed a way into his heart. I just know it. <br /><br />Mac goes through a lot in this installment. Thankfully it’s not detailed bit by bit, because I can’t take that sort of thing. At the end of Bloodfever there’s a lot of unanswered questions <i>but</i> I was able to pop in the next book, Faefever, right after finishing, so I’m not going to complain! <br /><br />I have to say, when I first started listening to this audio I wasn’t pleased that it was a woman narrating every voice, even Barrons, but now that I’ve been listening to it, I don’t mind. I love the southern voice for Mac, it’s pitch perfect. Faefever is the same narrator, Joyce Bean, and I love it already. I’m curious how the last two are going to sound. There is a switch to a male and female narrator and I’m excited! I’ve heard only good things about the male narrator. Can’t wait! <br /><br />I've been listening to the audio CD's to and from work. Finally, my commute time doesn't seem like such a waste. <br /><br />You can find this review and more at <a href="http://thereadersden.blogspot.com/2012/11/review-bloodfever-by-karen-marie-moning.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readers Den.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2014586936883422142" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vgxqNn3zsvflZ+MOWFreGi7RykInOFWBOh9HX3fMzdCEKgPkxq17n0JMV2+vr9TF+I4tium12+ZhYQHuuo8/Sg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AL0qdqX+hUAm5m0wOIXHO9VFlY5tTmULd9I1apdv5z06m0OkHqBMKIHN2VHPcM3kAxpyRqPD62wsrHPbWiwVpw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17011306069366899039">“The only other calling I ever felt was an irrepressible desire to be Captain of my own Starship. I was born in the wrong century and it wasn’t possible, so I chose to explore the universe by writing fiction instead. Books are doors to endless adventure.” -KMM<br/><br/>Karen Marie Moning is the #1 NYT bestselling author of the Fever Series and Highlander novels.<br/><br/>An alum of the Immaculate Conception Academy, </span>
  <span id="freeText17011306069366899039" style="display:none">“The only other calling I ever felt was an irrepressible desire to be Captain of my own Starship. I was born in the wrong century and it wasn’t possible, so I chose to explore the universe by writing fiction instead. Books are doors to endless adventure.” -KMM<br /><br />Karen Marie Moning is the #1 NYT bestselling author of the Fever Series and Highlander novels.<br /><br />An alum of the Immaculate Conception Academy, at seventeen she attended Purdue University where she completed a BA in Society &amp; Law, with minors in Philosophy, Creative Writing and Theatre, while working full time as a bartender and computer consultant. She intended to go to law school but after an internship with a firm of Criminal Attorneys, decided against it. For the next decade, she worked in insurance, where she wrote intercompany arbitrations and directed commercial litigation. At the age of thirty, she decided it was time to get serious and do what she’d always wanted to do: write fiction novels.<br /><br />Beyond the Highland Mist was published in 1999 and nominated for two RITA awards. She then published six more novels in her award-winning HIGHLANDER series, and received the RITA Award in 2001 for The Highlander’s Touch.<br /><br />In 2004, she began writing the #1 New York Times bestselling FEVER series. The books have been optioned twice for potential franchise development by Twentieth Century Fox and DreamWorks Studios, but the rights are currently held by Moning who has expressed a desire to one day see it as a television series. Her novels have been published in over thirty countries. She divides her time between Ohio and Florida and is working on two future projects for Random House Publishing.<br /><br />“I have always imagined that Paradise will be a kind of library.” – Jorge Luis Borges</span>
